## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / kinetic ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of a concentration A, which is the standard formulation of chemical kinetics via rate laws (ordinary differential equations). With only t and A available, the most common mechanistic structures are order-based decay/production terms in A, optionally with explicit time-varying rate coefficients or source/sink terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion, e.g., surface-limited or excess-reactant regimes)
- Zero-order production / source: dA_dt = c0 (constant feed or generation term)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive-like, many elementary steps under pseudo-first-order conditions)
- First-order with source (CSTR-like or generation-loss): dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (balance between constant input and linear loss)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular 2A→products or A+B with B≈A)
- General n-th order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical/global kinetics with non-integer order)
- Autocatalytic growth/decay (quadratic feedback): dA_dt = c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (self-amplification with depletion/inhibition by A)
- Reversible approach-to-equilibrium (linear relaxation): dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (net forward/backward giving exponential approach to equilibrium concentration c1)
- Reversible with nonlinear forward term: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 + c2 * (c3 - A)**c4 (two opposing processes with different effective orders)
- Time-dependent first-order (e.g., temperature/programmed-rate effects): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (rate coefficient varying approximately linearly in time)
- Exponentially time-varying rate coefficient: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (accelerating/decelerating kinetics due to external forcing)
- Saturating/inhibited decay (empirical): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate tends to -c0 at high A; can mimic capacity-limited removal)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elementary-order identification: linear in A suggests first-order; quadratic in A suggests bimolecular/second-order; non-integer power A**c indicates effective/global order.
- Sign constraints from chemistry: for pure consumption, dA_dt should be ≤ 0 for A > 0; production terms appear as additive positive sources.
- Equilibrium relaxation: structures proportional to (c - A) imply a stable fixed point A = c (approach to equilibrium).
- Competing pathways: sums of multiple negative terms (e.g., -k1*A - k2*A**2) indicate parallel consumption channels with different orders.
- Autocatalysis/feedback: presence of both +A and -A**2 terms indicates self-accelerating behavior at low A with self-limitation at high A.
- Time-varying environment: explicit dependence on t in the effective rate coefficient (k(t)) indicates external forcing (temperature ramps, illumination schedules, catalyst activation/deactivation).
- Capacity limitation: rational forms like A/(A+c) produce near-linear behavior at low A and plateauing rate at high A (transport/catalyst site limitations).
- Positivity/physical feasibility: models should avoid driving A negative; stable kinetics often have dA_dt→0 as A→0 for pure decay (e.g., -k*A^n with n>0).

GT: -c0*A**c1 + c2*_q*A*log(c3*t + c4)
Candidate formulas: 50

GT is the fixed function of two variables \(t,A\):
\[
f(t,A)= -0.1149290460\,A^2 \;+\; 0.06806555110\,A\;\log(0.2569297861\,t+1).
\]
Key structural facts:
- It has an \(A^2\) term with a fixed nonzero coefficient.
- Its only \(t\)-dependence is through \(\log(\alpha t+1)\), multiplied by \(A\).
- There is **no** plain \(A\) term, no constant term, no \(\exp(\cdot)\), no \(\sqrt{|A|}\), no \(\max(0,A)\), no \(|A|^p\) (unless \(p=1\) etc.), and no rational-in-\(A\) terms.
So any matching candidate must be able to reduce *exactly* to “quadratic in \(A\) + \(A\log(\text{affine in }t)\)” with nothing else.

Now check each candidate (constants in candidates are free to set, but the functional forms present cannot be changed).

1. Contains \(A c_2 e^{c_3 t}\), rational terms in \(A\), \(\sqrt{|A|}\), and \(A^{-1/4}\). These cannot be turned into \(A\log(\alpha t+1)\) for all \(t\). Setting their coefficients to 0 removes them, but then no \(A\log(\cdot)\) remains. **No match**.

2. Has \(A c_2 e^{c_3 t}\), \(e^{c_5 t}\max(0,A)\), \(|A|^{c_7}\). No log-in-\(t\) term. **No match**.

Also there is an unavoidable \(\sqrt{|A|}\) term (no coefficient to zero it). GT has none. **No match**.

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK4)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A**c1 + c2*_q*A*log(c3*t + c4)
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: -0.11493·A² + 0.06807·A·log(0.25693·t + 1)**

The GT has two terms:
1. A term proportional to A²
2. A term proportional to A·log(linear function of t)

Key structural features:
- The GT involves A² and A·log(c·t + 1)
- No exponential terms in t or A
- No sqrt, abs, max, sin, or other nonlinear functions of A alone

Let me analyze each candidate systematically. For a candidate to match, it must be able to produce exactly A² and A·log(c·t+1) terms, with all other terms zeroed out.

**Critical observation:** Most candidates contain terms like `A*c*exp(c*t)`. The term `A·exp(c·t)` is NOT equivalent to `A·log(c·t+1)` for any constant choices. These are fundamentally different basis functions. Setting the coefficient to 0 would eliminate the only t-dependent term, but the GT requires a t-dependent term.

Let me check which candidates have `A·log(...)` terms or other structures that could produce `A·log(c·t+1)`:

Going through all candidates:

- **Candidates 1-14, 17-50**: These use `exp(c*t)` as the t-dependent coupling with A, or have no log terms. Since exp(c·t) ≠ log(c·t+1), and we can't set the exp coefficient to 0 (we'd lose t-dependence), these cannot match.

- **Candidate 15**: `A²c0 + Ac1 + Ac2·exp(c3·t) + c4·log(Ac5+1) + c6 + c7·log(c8·log(Ac9+1)+1)` — Has log terms but they depend on A, not on t coupled with A. The t-dependence is only through exp. No match.

- **Candidate 16**: `A²c0 + Ac1 + Ac2·exp(c3·t) + c4·log(Ac5+1) + c6` — Same issue: log depends on A only, t-dependence through exp only. No match.

- **Candidate 19**: `A²c0 + Ac1 + Ac2·exp(c3·t) + c4 + c5·log(c6·t+1)·|A|^c7 + √|A|`
  This has `log(c6·t+1)·|A|^c7`. With A ≥ 0, |A| = A. Set c7 = 1: this becomes `c5·A·log(c6·t+1)`. Set c2 = 0 (kill exp term), set c1 = 0, c4 = 0, and set sqrt(|A|) — but sqrt(|A|) = √A cannot be zeroed since it has no coefficient. **No match** (can't eliminate √A).

- **Candidate 21**: `A²c0 + Ac1 + Ac2·exp(c3·t) + c4·|A|^c5 + c6 + c7·exp(c8·|A|)·log(c9·t+1)`
  Has `exp(c8·|A|)·log(c9·t+1)`. With A ≥ 0, set c8 = 0: this becomes `c7·log(c9·t+1)`, which is not multiplied by A. We need A·log(...). Can't get that structure. **No match.**

- **Candidate 28**: `A²c0 + Ac1 + Ac2·(c3+t)^c4 + A^c5 + A^c6·c7·exp(c8·t) + c9`
  Has `A·c2·(c3+t)^c4`. This is a power of t, not log. **No match.**

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates can produce the exact form A·log(c·t+1) that the GT requires, because they either lack log terms entirely, have log terms not coupled with A in the right way, or have extra terms that cannot be zeroed.

Candidate 1-50 verdict: [NO MATCH] for all.
